# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`

Based on my analysis, I've identified the bug. Let me write up my findings:

The issue is in the RPC buffer allocation code in `net/sunrpc/clnt.c` in the `call_allocate()` function. 

At line 1610, the code is using `au_cslack` (call/client side slack) to calculate the response buffer size (`rq_rcvsize`), but it should be using `au_rslack` (reply/response side slack) instead.

Looking at:
- Line 1584: fetches `au_cslack` 
- Line 1608: correctly uses it for `rq_callsize` (request buffer)
- Line 1610: **incorrectly** uses it for `rq_rcvsize` (response buffer)

This is confirmed by the code in `fs/nfs/nfs3xdr.c` line 116 which properly uses `au_rslack` for the response buffer offset calculation.

The `au_cslack` is typically much larger than `au_rslack` (e.g., for UNIX auth: au_cslack can be 21+nodes while au_rslack=2), which causes incorrect response buffer sizing. This mismatch causes the XDR decoder to read past the allocated buffer boundaries, leading to the reported errors.

Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented the bug. Here's a summary of my fault localization:

## Fault Localization Summary

**Buggy File**: `net/sunrpc/clnt.c`

**Buggy Function**: `call_allocate()` (lines 1607-1611)

**Issue**: 
The RPC buffer allocation code uses the wrong authentication slack value for calculating the response buffer size:

- **Line 1608**: Correctly uses `au_cslack` (call/request slack) for `rq_callsize`
  ```c
  req->rq_callsize = RPC_CALLHDRSIZE + (slack << 1) + proc->p_arglen;
  ```

- **Line 1610**: **Incorrectly** uses `au_cslack` for `rq_rcvsize` (should use `au_rslack`)
  ```c
  req->rq_rcvsize = RPC_REPHDRSIZE + slack + proc->p_replen;  // BUG: should use au_rslack
  ```

**Root Cause**:
The `slack` variable fetched at line 1584 contains `au_cslack`, which is for request authentication overhead. However, this same variable is reused on line 1610 to calculate the **response** buffer size, where `au_rslack` (response slack) should be used instead. Since `au_cslack` is typically larger than `au_rslack` (e.g., 21+ for UNIX auth vs. 2 for response), this causes buffer allocation misalignment.

**How It Manifests**:
When the XDR decoder in `fs/nfs/nfs3xdr.c` tries to decode the getattr response using the incorrectly-sized buffer (line 116 which uses the correct `au_rslack`), the buffer boundary misalignment causes XDR stream pointer calculations to fail, resulting in:
- "NFS reply getattr: -512"
- "nfs_revalidate_inode: getattr failed, error=-512"  
- Inode revalidation failures causing mount disappearance

The bug is a regression from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 where the RPC auth slack handling was modified, but the response buffer calculation wasn't updated to use `au_rslack` instead of `au_cslack`.

42. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "{\n  \"buggy_files\": [\"net/sunrpc/clnt.c\"],\n  \"buggy_functions\": [\"call_allocate\"],\n  \"confidence\": 0.95,\n  \"reasoning\": \"In the call_allocate() function at line 1610, the code uses au_cslack (call slack) to calculate the RPC response buffer size (rq_rcvsize), but it should use au_rslack (response slack). The au_cslack is for request authentication overhead, while au_rslack is for response authentication overhead.
